<s> dubourg you will be introduced to a set of acquaintance all friends to the americans <\s>
<s> by conversing with them you will have a good opportunity of acquiring parisian french and you will find in m <\s>
<s> dubourg a man prudent faithful secret intelligent in affairs and capable of giving you very sage advice <\s>
<s> it is scarce necessary to pretend any other business at paris than the gratifying of that curiosity which draws numbers thither yearly merely to see so famous a city <\s>
<s> with the assistance of monsieur dubourg who understands english you will be able to make immediate application to monsieur de vergennes _ministre des affaires etrangères either personally or by letter if m <\s>
<s> dubourg adopts that method acquainting him that you are in france upon business of the american congress in the character of a merchant having something to communicate to him that may be mutually beneficial to france and the north american colonies that you request an audience of him and that he would be pleased to appoint the time and place <\s>
<s> at this audience if agreed to it may be well to show him first your letter of credence and then acquaint him that the congress finding that in the common course of commerce it was not practicable to furnish the continent of america with the quantity of arms and ammunition necessary for its defence the ministry of great britain having been extremely industrious to prevent it you had been despatched by their authority to apply to some european power for a supply <\s>
<s> that france had been pitched on for the first application from an opinion that if we should as there is a great appearance we shall come to a total separation from great britain france would be looked upon as the power whose friendship it would be fittest for us to obtain and cultivate <\s>
<s> that the commercial advantages britain had enjoyed with the colonies had contributed greatly to her late wealth and importance <\s>
<s> that it is likely great part of our commerce will naturally fall to the share of france especially if she favors us in this application as that will be a means of gaining and securing the friendship of the colonies and that as our trade was rapidly increasing with our increase of people and in a greater proportion her part of it will be extremely valuable <\s>
<s> that the supply we at present want is clothing and arms for twenty five thousand men with a suitable quantity of ammunition and one hundred field pieces <\s>
<s> that we mean to pay for the same by remittances to france or through spain portugal or the french islands as soon as our navigation can be protected by ourselves or friends and that we besides want great quantities of linens and woollens with other articles for the indian trade which you are now actually purchasing and for which you ask no credit and that the whole if france should grant the other supplies would make a cargo which it might be well to secure by a convoy of two or three ships of war <\s>
<s> if you should find m <\s>
<s> de vergennes reserved and not inclined to enter into free conversation with you it may be well to shorten your visit request him to consider what you have proposed acquaint him with your place of lodging that you may yet stay sometime at paris and that knowing how precious his time is you do not presume to ask another audience but that if he should have any commands for you you will upon the least notice immediately wait upon him <\s>
<s> if at a future conference he should be more free and you find a disposition to favor the colonies it may be proper to acquaint him that they must necessarily be anxious to know the disposition of france on certain points which with his permission you would mention such as whether if the colonies should be forced to form themselves into an independent state france would probably acknowledge them as such receive their ambassadors enter into any treaty or alliance with them for commerce or defence or both <\s>
<s> if so on what principal conditions <\s>
<s> intimating that you shall speedily have an opportunity of sending to america if you do not immediately return and that he may be assured of your fidelity and secrecy in transmitting carefully any thing he would wish conveyed to the congress on that subject <\s>
<s> in subsequent conversations you may as you find it convenient enlarge on these topics that have been the subjects of our conferences with you to which you may occasionally add the well known substantial answers we usually give to the several calumnies thrown out against us <\s>
<s> if these supplies on the credit of the congress should be refused you are then to endeavor the obtaining a permission of purchasing those articles or as much of them as you can find credit for <\s>
<s> you will keep a daily journal of all your material transactions and particularly of what passes in your conversation with great personages and you will by every safe opportunity furnish us with such information as may be important <\s>
<s> when your business in france admits of it it may be well to go into holland and visit our agent there m <\s>

<s> dubourg you will be introduced to a set of acquaintance all friends to the americans <\s>
<s> by conversing with them you will have a good opportunity of acquiring parisian french and you will find in m <\s>
<s> dubourg a man prudent faithful secret intelligent in affairs and capable of giving you very sage advice <\s>
<s> it is scarce necessary to pretend any other business at paris than the gratifying of that curiosity which draws numbers thither yearly merely to see so famous a city <\s>
<s> with the assistance of monsieur dubourg who understands english you will be able to make immediate application to monsieur de vergennes _ministre des affaires etrangères either personally or by letter if m <\s>
<s> dubourg adopts that method acquainting him that you are in france upon business of the american congress in the character of a merchant having something to communicate to him that may be mutually beneficial to france and the north american colonies that you request an audience of him and that he would be pleased to appoint the time and place <\s>
<s> at this audience if agreed to it may be well to show him first your letter of credence and then acquaint him that the congress finding that in the common course of commerce it was not practicable to furnish the continent of america with the quantity of arms and ammunition necessary for its defence the ministry of great britain having been extremely industrious to prevent it you had been despatched by their authority to apply to some european power for a supply <\s>
<s> that france had been pitched on for the first application from an opinion that if we should as there is a great appearance we shall come to a total separation from great britain france would be looked upon as the power whose friendship it would be fittest for us to obtain and cultivate <\s>
<s> that the commercial advantages britain had enjoyed with the colonies had contributed greatly to her late wealth and importance <\s>
<s> that it is likely great part of our commerce will naturally fall to the share of france especially if she favors us in this application as that will be a means of gaining and securing the friendship of the colonies and that as our trade was rapidly increasing with our increase of people and in a greater proportion her part of it will be extremely valuable <\s>
<s> that the supply we at present want is clothing and arms for twenty five thousand men with a suitable quantity of ammunition and one hundred field pieces <\s>
<s> that we mean to pay for the same by remittances to france or through spain portugal or the french islands as soon as our navigation can be protected by ourselves or friends and that we besides want great quantities of linens and woollens with other articles for the indian trade which you are now actually purchasing and for which you ask no credit and that the whole if france should grant the other supplies would make a cargo which it might be well to secure by a convoy of two or three ships of war <\s>
<s> if you should find m <\s>
<s> de vergennes reserved and not inclined to enter into free conversation with you it may be well to shorten your visit request him to consider what you have proposed acquaint him with your place of lodging that you may yet stay sometime at paris and that knowing how precious his time is you do not presume to ask another audience but that if he should have any commands for you you will upon the least notice immediately wait upon him <\s>
<s> if at a future conference he should be more free and you find a disposition to favor the colonies it may be proper to acquaint him that they must necessarily be anxious to know the disposition of france on certain points which with his permission you would mention such as whether if the colonies should be forced to form themselves into an independent state france would probably acknowledge them as such receive their ambassadors enter into any treaty or alliance with them for commerce or defence or both <\s>
<s> if so on what principal conditions <\s>
<s> intimating that you shall speedily have an opportunity of sending to america if you do not immediately return and that he may be assured of your fidelity and secrecy in transmitting carefully any thing he would wish conveyed to the congress on that subject <\s>
<s> in subsequent conversations you may as you find it convenient enlarge on these topics that have been the subjects of our conferences with you to which you may occasionally add the well known substantial answers we usually give to the several calumnies thrown out against us <\s>
<s> if these supplies on the credit of the congress should be refused you are then to endeavor the obtaining a permission of purchasing those articles or as much of them as you can find credit for <\s>
<s> you will keep a daily journal of all your material transactions and particularly of what passes in your conversation with great personages and you will by every safe opportunity furnish us with such information as may be important <\s>
<s> when your business in france admits of it it may be well to go into holland and visit our agent there m <\s>

<s> passy february 10th 1779 513 note the french money so often mentioned in this and the succeeding volumes is reckoned in livres sols and deniers <\s>
<s> thus 85,706 _l 16_s 3_d or 85,706 <\s>
<s> indicates 85,706 livres 16 sols 3 deniers <\s>
<s> in reducing this money to american currency five livres and eight sols were allowed to the dollar <\s>
<s> the correspondence of silas deane commissioner from the united states to the court of france <\s>
<s> silas deane was born in the town of groton connecticut and graduated at yale college in 1758 <\s>
<s> he was a member from his native colony of the first congress that met in philadelphia <\s>
<s> early in the year 1776 the committee of secret correspondence commissioned him to go to france as a political and commercial agent <\s>
<s> he was instructed to ascertain the disposition of the french court in regard to the contest between great britain and the colonies and to procure if possible supplies of arms and military stores <\s>
<s> having arrived at paris in june he immediately applied himself to execute his instructions and was successful in obtaining the main objects for which he was sent <\s>
<s> in september three commissioners were appointed by congress to negotiate treaties with foreign powers and particularly with the court of france <\s>
<s> the persons chosen were dr franklin silas deane and arthur lee <\s>
<s> they all met at paris in december and continued to procure supplies of money and arms for the united states till at length they signed the treaties of alliance and commerce with france february 6th 1778 <\s>
<s> meantime deane had been recalled on the 21st of november preceding <\s>
<s> of this he received the intelligence in march following and left paris april 1st to join count d'estaing's fleet at toulon in which he came to america <\s>
<s> the account which he gave to congress of his transactions abroad was not satisfactory and he was detained many months in philadelphia soliciting opportunities to vindicate himself before congress from what he deemed the unjust charges of his enemies but the papers relating to his mercantile proceedings having been left in france he was not able wholly to remove the unfavorable impression that existed against him <\s>
<s> congress however neither passed a vote of censure nor approbation of his conduct <\s>
<s> in the spring of 1780 he returned to france where he remained more than a year in reduced circumstances attempting to settle his accounts <\s>
<s> he exhibited large claims against congress which do not appear to have been allowed <\s>
<s> in march 1782 he was living in ghent <\s>
<s> after the peace he went to england where he died in august 1789 <\s>
<s> the correspondence of silas deane <\s>
<s> from the committee of secret correspondence to silas deane 1 philadelphia march 3d 1776 <\s>
<s> on your arrival in france you will for some time be engaged in the business of providing goods for the indian trade <\s>
<s> this will give good countenance to your appearing in the character of a merchant which we wish you continually to retain among the french in general it being probable that the court of france may not like it should be known publicly that any agent from the colonies is in that country <\s>
<s> when you come to paris by delivering dr franklin's letters to monsieur le roy at the louvre and m <\s>
<s> dubourg you will be introduced to a set of acquaintance all friends to the americans <\s>
<s> by conversing with them you will have a good opportunity of acquiring parisian french and you will find in m <\s>
<s> dubourg a man prudent faithful secret intelligent in affairs and capable of giving you very sage advice <\s>
<s> it is scarce necessary to pretend any other business at paris than the gratifying of that curiosity which draws numbers thither yearly merely to see so famous a city <\s>
<s> with the assistance of monsieur dubourg who understands english you will be able to make immediate application to monsieur de vergennes _ministre des affaires etrangères either personally or by letter if m <\s>
<s> dubourg adopts that method acquainting him that you are in france upon business of the american congress in the character of a merchant having something to communicate to him that may be mutually beneficial to france and the north american colonies that you request an audience of him and that he would be pleased to appoint the time and place <\s>
<s> at this audience if agreed to it may be well to show him first your letter of credence and then acquaint him that the congress finding that in the common course of commerce it was not practicable to furnish the continent of america with the quantity of arms and ammunition necessary for its defence the ministry of great britain having been extremely industrious to prevent it you had been despatched by their authority to apply to some european power for a supply <\s>
<s> that france had been pitched on for the first application from an opinion that if we should as there is a great appearance we shall come to a total separation from great britain france would be looked upon as the power whose friendship it would be fittest for us to obtain and cultivate <\s>
<s> that the commercial advantages britain had enjoyed with the colonies had contributed greatly to her late wealth and importance <\s>
<s> that it is likely great part of our commerce will naturally fall to the share of france especially if she favors us in this application as that will be a means of gaining and securing the friendship of the colonies and that as our trade was rapidly increasing with our increase of people and in a greater proportion her part of it will be extremely valuable <\s>
<s> that the supply we at present want is clothing and arms for twenty five thousand men with a suitable quantity of ammunition and one hundred field pieces <\s>
<s> that we mean to pay for the same by remittances to france or through spain portugal or the french islands as soon as our navigation can be protected by ourselves or friends and that we besides want great quantities of linens and woollens with other articles for the indian trade which you are now actually purchasing and for which you ask no credit and that the whole if france should grant the other supplies would make a cargo which it might be well to secure by a convoy of two or three ships of war <\s>
<s> if you should find m <\s>
<s> de vergennes reserved and not inclined to enter into free conversation with you it may be well to shorten your visit request him to consider what you have proposed acquaint him with your place of lodging that you may yet stay sometime at paris and that knowing how precious his time is you do not presume to ask another audience but that if he should have any commands for you you will upon the least notice immediately wait upon him <\s>
<s> if at a future conference he should be more free and you find a disposition to favor the colonies it may be proper to acquaint him that they must necessarily be anxious to know the disposition of france on certain points which with his permission you would mention such as whether if the colonies should be forced to form themselves into an independent state france would probably acknowledge them as such receive their ambassadors enter into any treaty or alliance with them for commerce or defence or both <\s>
<s> if so on what principal conditions <\s>
<s> intimating that you shall speedily have an opportunity of sending to america if you do not immediately return and that he may be assured of your fidelity and secrecy in transmitting carefully any thing he would wish conveyed to the congress on that subject <\s>
<s> in subsequent conversations you may as you find it convenient enlarge on these topics that have been the subjects of our conferences with you to which you may occasionally add the well known substantial answers we usually give to the several calumnies thrown out against us <\s>
<s> if these supplies on the credit of the congress should be refused you are then to endeavor the obtaining a permission of purchasing those articles or as much of them as you can find credit for <\s>
<s> you will keep a daily journal of all your material transactions and particularly of what passes in your conversation with great personages and you will by every safe opportunity furnish us with such information as may be important <\s>
<s> when your business in france admits of it it may be well to go into holland and visit our agent there m <\s>

<s> passy february 10th 1779 513 note the french money so often mentioned in this and the succeeding volumes is reckoned in livres sols and deniers <\s>
<s> thus 85,706 _l 16_s 3_d or 85,706 <\s>
<s> indicates 85,706 livres 16 sols 3 deniers <\s>
<s> in reducing this money to american currency five livres and eight sols were allowed to the dollar <\s>
<s> the correspondence of silas deane commissioner from the united states to the court of france <\s>
<s> silas deane was born in the town of groton connecticut and graduated at yale college in 1758 <\s>
<s> he was a member from his native colony of the first congress that met in philadelphia <\s>
<s> early in the year 1776 the committee of secret correspondence commissioned him to go to france as a political and commercial agent <\s>
<s> he was instructed to ascertain the disposition of the french court in regard to the contest between great britain and the colonies and to procure if possible supplies of arms and military stores <\s>
<s> having arrived at paris in june he immediately applied himself to execute his instructions and was successful in obtaining the main objects for which he was sent <\s>
<s> in september three commissioners were appointed by congress to negotiate treaties with foreign powers and particularly with the court of france <\s>
<s> the persons chosen were dr franklin silas deane and arthur lee <\s>
<s> they all met at paris in december and continued to procure supplies of money and arms for the united states till at length they signed the treaties of alliance and commerce with france february 6th 1778 <\s>
<s> meantime deane had been recalled on the 21st of november preceding <\s>
<s> of this he received the intelligence in march following and left paris april 1st to join count d'estaing's fleet at toulon in which he came to america <\s>
<s> the account which he gave to congress of his transactions abroad was not satisfactory and he was detained many months in philadelphia soliciting opportunities to vindicate himself before congress from what he deemed the unjust charges of his enemies but the papers relating to his mercantile proceedings having been left in france he was not able wholly to remove the unfavorable impression that existed against him <\s>
<s> congress however neither passed a vote of censure nor approbation of his conduct <\s>
<s> in the spring of 1780 he returned to france where he remained more than a year in reduced circumstances attempting to settle his accounts <\s>
<s> he exhibited large claims against congress which do not appear to have been allowed <\s>
<s> in march 1782 he was living in ghent <\s>
<s> after the peace he went to england where he died in august 1789 <\s>
<s> the correspondence of silas deane <\s>
<s> from the committee of secret correspondence to silas deane 1 philadelphia march 3d 1776 <\s>
<s> on your arrival in france you will for some time be engaged in the business of providing goods for the indian trade <\s>
<s> this will give good countenance to your appearing in the character of a merchant which we wish you continually to retain among the french in general it being probable that the court of france may not like it should be known publicly that any agent from the colonies is in that country <\s>
<s> when you come to paris by delivering dr franklin's letters to monsieur le roy at the louvre and m <\s>
<s> dubourg you will be introduced to a set of acquaintance all friends to the americans <\s>
<s> by conversing with them you will have a good opportunity of acquiring parisian french and you will find in m <\s>
<s> dubourg a man prudent faithful secret intelligent in affairs and capable of giving you very sage advice <\s>
<s> it is scarce necessary to pretend any other business at paris than the gratifying of that curiosity which draws numbers thither yearly merely to see so famous a city <\s>
<s> with the assistance of monsieur dubourg who understands english you will be able to make immediate application to monsieur de vergennes _ministre des affaires etrangères either personally or by letter if m <\s>
<s> dubourg adopts that method acquainting him that you are in france upon business of the american congress in the character of a merchant having something to communicate to him that may be mutually beneficial to france and the north american colonies that you request an audience of him and that he would be pleased to appoint the time and place <\s>
<s> at this audience if agreed to it may be well to show him first your letter of credence and then acquaint him that the congress finding that in the common course of commerce it was not practicable to furnish the continent of america with the quantity of arms and ammunition necessary for its defence the ministry of great britain having been extremely industrious to prevent it you had been despatched by their authority to apply to some european power for a supply <\s>
<s> that france had been pitched on for the first application from an opinion that if we should as there is a great appearance we shall come to a total separation from great britain france would be looked upon as the power whose friendship it would be fittest for us to obtain and cultivate <\s>
<s> that the commercial advantages britain had enjoyed with the colonies had contributed greatly to her late wealth and importance <\s>
<s> that it is likely great part of our commerce will naturally fall to the share of france especially if she favors us in this application as that will be a means of gaining and securing the friendship of the colonies and that as our trade was rapidly increasing with our increase of people and in a greater proportion her part of it will be extremely valuable <\s>
<s> that the supply we at present want is clothing and arms for twenty five thousand men with a suitable quantity of ammunition and one hundred field pieces <\s>
<s> that we mean to pay for the same by remittances to france or through spain portugal or the french islands as soon as our navigation can be protected by ourselves or friends and that we besides want great quantities of linens and woollens with other articles for the indian trade which you are now actually purchasing and for which you ask no credit and that the whole if france should grant the other supplies would make a cargo which it might be well to secure by a convoy of two or three ships of war <\s>
<s> if you should find m <\s>
<s> de vergennes reserved and not inclined to enter into free conversation with you it may be well to shorten your visit request him to consider what you have proposed acquaint him with your place of lodging that you may yet stay sometime at paris and that knowing how precious his time is you do not presume to ask another audience but that if he should have any commands for you you will upon the least notice immediately wait upon him <\s>
<s> if at a future conference he should be more free and you find a disposition to favor the colonies it may be proper to acquaint him that they must necessarily be anxious to know the disposition of france on certain points which with his permission you would mention such as whether if the colonies should be forced to form themselves into an independent state france would probably acknowledge them as such receive their ambassadors enter into any treaty or alliance with them for commerce or defence or both <\s>
<s> if so on what principal conditions <\s>
<s> intimating that you shall speedily have an opportunity of sending to america if you do not immediately return and that he may be assured of your fidelity and secrecy in transmitting carefully any thing he would wish conveyed to the congress on that subject <\s>
<s> in subsequent conversations you may as you find it convenient enlarge on these topics that have been the subjects of our conferences with you to which you may occasionally add the well known substantial answers we usually give to the several calumnies thrown out against us <\s>
<s> if these supplies on the credit of the congress should be refused you are then to endeavor the obtaining a permission of purchasing those articles or as much of them as you can find credit for <\s>
<s> you will keep a daily journal of all your material transactions and particularly of what passes in your conversation with great personages and you will by every safe opportunity furnish us with such information as may be important <\s>
<s> when your business in france admits of it it may be well to go into holland and visit our agent there m <\s>

<s> he was a member from his native colony of the first congress that met in philadelphia <\s>
<s> early in the year 1776 the committee of secret correspondence commissioned him to go to france as a political and commercial agent <\s>
<s> he was instructed to ascertain the disposition of the french court in regard to the contest between great britain and the colonies and to procure if possible supplies of arms and military stores <\s>
<s> having arrived at paris in june he immediately applied himself to execute his instructions and was successful in obtaining the main objects for which he was sent <\s>
<s> in september three commissioners were appointed by congress to negotiate treaties with foreign powers and particularly with the court of france <\s>
<s> the persons chosen were dr franklin silas deane and arthur lee <\s>
<s> they all met at paris in december and continued to procure supplies of money and arms for the united states till at length they signed the treaties of alliance and commerce with france february 6th 1778 <\s>
<s> meantime deane had been recalled on the 21st of november preceding <\s>
<s> of this he received the intelligence in march following and left paris april 1st to join count d'estaing's fleet at toulon in which he came to america <\s>
<s> the account which he gave to congress of his transactions abroad was not satisfactory and he was detained many months in philadelphia soliciting opportunities to vindicate himself before congress from what he deemed the unjust charges of his enemies but the papers relating to his mercantile proceedings having been left in france he was not able wholly to remove the unfavorable impression that existed against him <\s>
<s> congress however neither passed a vote of censure nor approbation of his conduct <\s>
<s> in the spring of 1780 he returned to france where he remained more than a year in reduced circumstances attempting to settle his accounts <\s>
<s> he exhibited large claims against congress which do not appear to have been allowed <\s>
<s> in march 1782 he was living in ghent <\s>
<s> after the peace he went to england where he died in august 1789 <\s>
<s> the correspondence of silas deane <\s>
<s> from the committee of secret correspondence to silas deane 1 philadelphia march 3d 1776 <\s>
<s> on your arrival in france you will for some time be engaged in the business of providing goods for the indian trade <\s>
<s> this will give good countenance to your appearing in the character of a merchant which we wish you continually to retain among the french in general it being probable that the court of france may not like it should be known publicly that any agent from the colonies is in that country <\s>
<s> when you come to paris by delivering dr franklin's letters to monsieur le roy at the louvre and m <\s>
<s> dubourg you will be introduced to a set of acquaintance all friends to the americans <\s>
<s> by conversing with them you will have a good opportunity of acquiring parisian french and you will find in m <\s>
<s> dubourg a man prudent faithful secret intelligent in affairs and capable of giving you very sage advice <\s>
<s> it is scarce necessary to pretend any other business at paris than the gratifying of that curiosity which draws numbers thither yearly merely to see so famous a city <\s>
<s> with the assistance of monsieur dubourg who understands english you will be able to make immediate application to monsieur de vergennes _ministre des affaires etrangères either personally or by letter if m <\s>
<s> dubourg adopts that method acquainting him that you are in france upon business of the american congress in the character of a merchant having something to communicate to him that may be mutually beneficial to france and the north american colonies that you request an audience of him and that he would be pleased to appoint the time and place <\s>
<s> at this audience if agreed to it may be well to show him first your letter of credence and then acquaint him that the congress finding that in the common course of commerce it was not practicable to furnish the continent of america with the quantity of arms and ammunition necessary for its defence the ministry of great britain having been extremely industrious to prevent it you had been despatched by their authority to apply to some european power for a supply <\s>
<s> that france had been pitched on for the first application from an opinion that if we should as there is a great appearance we shall come to a total separation from great britain france would be looked upon as the power whose friendship it would be fittest for us to obtain and cultivate <\s>
<s> that the commercial advantages britain had enjoyed with the colonies had contributed greatly to her late wealth and importance <\s>
<s> that it is likely great part of our commerce will naturally fall to the share of france especially if she favors us in this application as that will be a means of gaining and securing the friendship of the colonies and that as our trade was rapidly increasing with our increase of people and in a greater proportion her part of it will be extremely valuable <\s>
<s> that the supply we at present want is clothing and arms for twenty five thousand men with a suitable quantity of ammunition and one hundred field pieces <\s>
<s> that we mean to pay for the same by remittances to france or through spain portugal or the french islands as soon as our navigation can be protected by ourselves or friends and that we besides want great quantities of linens and woollens with other articles for the indian trade which you are now actually purchasing and for which you ask no credit and that the whole if france should grant the other supplies would make a cargo which it might be well to secure by a convoy of two or three ships of war <\s>
<s> if you should find m <\s>
<s> de vergennes reserved and not inclined to enter into free conversation with you it may be well to shorten your visit request him to consider what you have proposed acquaint him with your place of lodging that you may yet stay sometime at paris and that knowing how precious his time is you do not presume to ask another audience but that if he should have any commands for you you will upon the least notice immediately wait upon him <\s>
<s> if at a future conference he should be more free and you find a disposition to favor the colonies it may be proper to acquaint him that they must necessarily be anxious to know the disposition of france on certain points which with his permission you would mention such as whether if the colonies should be forced to form themselves into an independent state france would probably acknowledge them as such receive their ambassadors enter into any treaty or alliance with them for commerce or defence or both <\s>
<s> if so on what principal conditions <\s>
<s> intimating that you shall speedily have an opportunity of sending to america if you do not immediately return and that he may be assured of your fidelity and secrecy in transmitting carefully any thing he would wish conveyed to the congress on that subject <\s>
<s> in subsequent conversations you may as you find it convenient enlarge on these topics that have been the subjects of our conferences with you to which you may occasionally add the well known substantial answers we usually give to the several calumnies thrown out against us <\s>
<s> if these supplies on the credit of the congress should be refused you are then to endeavor the obtaining a permission of purchasing those articles or as much of them as you can find credit for <\s>
<s> you will keep a daily journal of all your material transactions and particularly of what passes in your conversation with great personages and you will by every safe opportunity furnish us with such information as may be important <\s>
<s> when your business in france admits of it it may be well to go into holland and visit our agent there m <\s>

<s> passy january 1st 1779 500 threats of the british commissioners to change the conduct of the war in america former severities object of this change congress declare that they will retaliate propriety of interference by france advantage of a strong french fleet in the american seas coalition of parties in england against the americans <\s>

<s> passy february 10th 1779 513 note the french money so often mentioned in this and the succeeding volumes is reckoned in livres sols and deniers <\s>
<s> thus 85,706 _l 16_s 3_d or 85,706 <\s>
<s> indicates 85,706 livres 16 sols 3 deniers <\s>
<s> in reducing this money to american currency five livres and eight sols were allowed to the dollar <\s>
<s> the correspondence of silas deane commissioner from the united states to the court of france <\s>
<s> silas deane was born in the town of groton connecticut and graduated at yale college in 1758 <\s>
<s> he was a member from his native colony of the first congress that met in philadelphia <\s>
<s> early in the year 1776 the committee of secret correspondence commissioned him to go to france as a political and commercial agent <\s>
<s> he was instructed to ascertain the disposition of the french court in regard to the contest between great britain and the colonies and to procure if possible supplies of arms and military stores <\s>
<s> having arrived at paris in june he immediately applied himself to execute his instructions and was successful in obtaining the main objects for which he was sent <\s>
<s> in september three commissioners were appointed by congress to negotiate treaties with foreign powers and particularly with the court of france <\s>
<s> the persons chosen were dr franklin silas deane and arthur lee <\s>
<s> they all met at paris in december and continued to procure supplies of money and arms for the united states till at length they signed the treaties of alliance and commerce with france february 6th 1778 <\s>
<s> meantime deane had been recalled on the 21st of november preceding <\s>
<s> of this he received the intelligence in march following and left paris april 1st to join count d'estaing's fleet at toulon in which he came to america <\s>
<s> the account which he gave to congress of his transactions abroad was not satisfactory and he was detained many months in philadelphia soliciting opportunities to vindicate himself before congress from what he deemed the unjust charges of his enemies but the papers relating to his mercantile proceedings having been left in france he was not able wholly to remove the unfavorable impression that existed against him <\s>
<s> congress however neither passed a vote of censure nor approbation of his conduct <\s>
<s> in the spring of 1780 he returned to france where he remained more than a year in reduced circumstances attempting to settle his accounts <\s>
<s> he exhibited large claims against congress which do not appear to have been allowed <\s>
<s> in march 1782 he was living in ghent <\s>
<s> after the peace he went to england where he died in august 1789 <\s>
<s> the correspondence of silas deane <\s>
<s> from the committee of secret correspondence to silas deane 1 philadelphia march 3d 1776 <\s>
<s> on your arrival in france you will for some time be engaged in the business of providing goods for the indian trade <\s>
<s> this will give good countenance to your appearing in the character of a merchant which we wish you continually to retain among the french in general it being probable that the court of france may not like it should be known publicly that any agent from the colonies is in that country <\s>
<s> when you come to paris by delivering dr franklin's letters to monsieur le roy at the louvre and m <\s>
<s> dubourg you will be introduced to a set of acquaintance all friends to the americans <\s>
<s> by conversing with them you will have a good opportunity of acquiring parisian french and you will find in m <\s>
<s> dubourg a man prudent faithful secret intelligent in affairs and capable of giving you very sage advice <\s>
<s> it is scarce necessary to pretend any other business at paris than the gratifying of that curiosity which draws numbers thither yearly merely to see so famous a city <\s>
<s> with the assistance of monsieur dubourg who understands english you will be able to make immediate application to monsieur de vergennes _ministre des affaires etrangères either personally or by letter if m <\s>
<s> dubourg adopts that method acquainting him that you are in france upon business of the american congress in the character of a merchant having something to communicate to him that may be mutually beneficial to france and the north american colonies that you request an audience of him and that he would be pleased to appoint the time and place <\s>
<s> at this audience if agreed to it may be well to show him first your letter of credence and then acquaint him that the congress finding that in the common course of commerce it was not practicable to furnish the continent of america with the quantity of arms and ammunition necessary for its defence the ministry of great britain having been extremely industrious to prevent it you had been despatched by their authority to apply to some european power for a supply <\s>
<s> that france had been pitched on for the first application from an opinion that if we should as there is a great appearance we shall come to a total separation from great britain france would be looked upon as the power whose friendship it would be fittest for us to obtain and cultivate <\s>
<s> that the commercial advantages britain had enjoyed with the colonies had contributed greatly to her late wealth and importance <\s>
<s> that it is likely great part of our commerce will naturally fall to the share of france especially if she favors us in this application as that will be a means of gaining and securing the friendship of the colonies and that as our trade was rapidly increasing with our increase of people and in a greater proportion her part of it will be extremely valuable <\s>
<s> that the supply we at present want is clothing and arms for twenty five thousand men with a suitable quantity of ammunition and one hundred field pieces <\s>
<s> that we mean to pay for the same by remittances to france or through spain portugal or the french islands as soon as our navigation can be protected by ourselves or friends and that we besides want great quantities of linens and woollens with other articles for the indian trade which you are now actually purchasing and for which you ask no credit and that the whole if france should grant the other supplies would make a cargo which it might be well to secure by a convoy of two or three ships of war <\s>
<s> if you should find m <\s>
<s> de vergennes reserved and not inclined to enter into free conversation with you it may be well to shorten your visit request him to consider what you have proposed acquaint him with your place of lodging that you may yet stay sometime at paris and that knowing how precious his time is you do not presume to ask another audience but that if he should have any commands for you you will upon the least notice immediately wait upon him <\s>
<s> if at a future conference he should be more free and you find a disposition to favor the colonies it may be proper to acquaint him that they must necessarily be anxious to know the disposition of france on certain points which with his permission you would mention such as whether if the colonies should be forced to form themselves into an independent state france would probably acknowledge them as such receive their ambassadors enter into any treaty or alliance with them for commerce or defence or both <\s>
<s> if so on what principal conditions <\s>
<s> intimating that you shall speedily have an opportunity of sending to america if you do not immediately return and that he may be assured of your fidelity and secrecy in transmitting carefully any thing he would wish conveyed to the congress on that subject <\s>
<s> in subsequent conversations you may as you find it convenient enlarge on these topics that have been the subjects of our conferences with you to which you may occasionally add the well known substantial answers we usually give to the several calumnies thrown out against us <\s>
<s> if these supplies on the credit of the congress should be refused you are then to endeavor the obtaining a permission of purchasing those articles or as much of them as you can find credit for <\s>
<s> you will keep a daily journal of all your material transactions and particularly of what passes in your conversation with great personages and you will by every safe opportunity furnish us with such information as may be important <\s>
<s> when your business in france admits of it it may be well to go into holland and visit our agent there m <\s>

<s> that we mean to pay for the same by remittances to france or through spain portugal or the french islands as soon as our navigation can be protected by ourselves or friends and that we besides want great quantities of linens and woollens with other articles for the indian trade which you are now actually purchasing and for which you ask no credit and that the whole if france should grant the other supplies would make a cargo which it might be well to secure by a convoy of two or three ships of war <\s>
<s> if you should find m <\s>
<s> de vergennes reserved and not inclined to enter into free conversation with you it may be well to shorten your visit request him to consider what you have proposed acquaint him with your place of lodging that you may yet stay sometime at paris and that knowing how precious his time is you do not presume to ask another audience but that if he should have any commands for you you will upon the least notice immediately wait upon him <\s>
<s> if at a future conference he should be more free and you find a disposition to favor the colonies it may be proper to acquaint him that they must necessarily be anxious to know the disposition of france on certain points which with his permission you would mention such as whether if the colonies should be forced to form themselves into an independent state france would probably acknowledge them as such receive their ambassadors enter into any treaty or alliance with them for commerce or defence or both <\s>
<s> if so on what principal conditions <\s>
<s> intimating that you shall speedily have an opportunity of sending to america if you do not immediately return and that he may be assured of your fidelity and secrecy in transmitting carefully any thing he would wish conveyed to the congress on that subject <\s>
<s> in subsequent conversations you may as you find it convenient enlarge on these topics that have been the subjects of our conferences with you to which you may occasionally add the well known substantial answers we usually give to the several calumnies thrown out against us <\s>
<s> if these supplies on the credit of the congress should be refused you are then to endeavor the obtaining a permission of purchasing those articles or as much of them as you can find credit for <\s>
<s> you will keep a daily journal of all your material transactions and particularly of what passes in your conversation with great personages and you will by every safe opportunity furnish us with such information as may be important <\s>
<s> when your business in france admits of it it may be well to go into holland and visit our agent there m <\s>

<s> passy february 10th 1779 513 note the french money so often mentioned in this and the succeeding volumes is reckoned in livres sols and deniers <\s>
<s> thus 85,706 _l 16_s 3_d or 85,706 <\s>
<s> indicates 85,706 livres 16 sols 3 deniers <\s>
<s> in reducing this money to american currency five livres and eight sols were allowed to the dollar <\s>
<s> the correspondence of silas deane commissioner from the united states to the court of france <\s>
<s> silas deane was born in the town of groton connecticut and graduated at yale college in 1758 <\s>
<s> he was a member from his native colony of the first congress that met in philadelphia <\s>
<s> early in the year 1776 the committee of secret correspondence commissioned him to go to france as a political and commercial agent <\s>
<s> he was instructed to ascertain the disposition of the french court in regard to the contest between great britain and the colonies and to procure if possible supplies of arms and military stores <\s>
<s> having arrived at paris in june he immediately applied himself to execute his instructions and was successful in obtaining the main objects for which he was sent <\s>
<s> in september three commissioners were appointed by congress to negotiate treaties with foreign powers and particularly with the court of france <\s>
<s> the persons chosen were dr franklin silas deane and arthur lee <\s>
<s> they all met at paris in december and continued to procure supplies of money and arms for the united states till at length they signed the treaties of alliance and commerce with france february 6th 1778 <\s>
<s> meantime deane had been recalled on the 21st of november preceding <\s>
<s> of this he received the intelligence in march following and left paris april 1st to join count d'estaing's fleet at toulon in which he came to america <\s>
<s> the account which he gave to congress of his transactions abroad was not satisfactory and he was detained many months in philadelphia soliciting opportunities to vindicate himself before congress from what he deemed the unjust charges of his enemies but the papers relating to his mercantile proceedings having been left in france he was not able wholly to remove the unfavorable impression that existed against him <\s>
<s> congress however neither passed a vote of censure nor approbation of his conduct <\s>
<s> in the spring of 1780 he returned to france where he remained more than a year in reduced circumstances attempting to settle his accounts <\s>
<s> he exhibited large claims against congress which do not appear to have been allowed <\s>
<s> in march 1782 he was living in ghent <\s>
<s> after the peace he went to england where he died in august 1789 <\s>
<s> the correspondence of silas deane <\s>
<s> from the committee of secret correspondence to silas deane 1 philadelphia march 3d 1776 <\s>
<s> on your arrival in france you will for some time be engaged in the business of providing goods for the indian trade <\s>
<s> this will give good countenance to your appearing in the character of a merchant which we wish you continually to retain among the french in general it being probable that the court of france may not like it should be known publicly that any agent from the colonies is in that country <\s>
<s> when you come to paris by delivering dr franklin's letters to monsieur le roy at the louvre and m <\s>
<s> dubourg you will be introduced to a set of acquaintance all friends to the americans <\s>
<s> by conversing with them you will have a good opportunity of acquiring parisian french and you will find in m <\s>
<s> dubourg a man prudent faithful secret intelligent in affairs and capable of giving you very sage advice <\s>
<s> it is scarce necessary to pretend any other business at paris than the gratifying of that curiosity which draws numbers thither yearly merely to see so famous a city <\s>
<s> with the assistance of monsieur dubourg who understands english you will be able to make immediate application to monsieur de vergennes _ministre des affaires etrangères either personally or by letter if m <\s>
<s> dubourg adopts that method acquainting him that you are in france upon business of the american congress in the character of a merchant having something to communicate to him that may be mutually beneficial to france and the north american colonies that you request an audience of him and that he would be pleased to appoint the time and place <\s>
<s> at this audience if agreed to it may be well to show him first your letter of credence and then acquaint him that the congress finding that in the common course of commerce it was not practicable to furnish the continent of america with the quantity of arms and ammunition necessary for its defence the ministry of great britain having been extremely industrious to prevent it you had been despatched by their authority to apply to some european power for a supply <\s>
<s> that france had been pitched on for the first application from an opinion that if we should as there is a great appearance we shall come to a total separation from great britain france would be looked upon as the power whose friendship it would be fittest for us to obtain and cultivate <\s>
<s> that the commercial advantages britain had enjoyed with the colonies had contributed greatly to her late wealth and importance <\s>
<s> that it is likely great part of our commerce will naturally fall to the share of france especially if she favors us in this application as that will be a means of gaining and securing the friendship of the colonies and that as our trade was rapidly increasing with our increase of people and in a greater proportion her part of it will be extremely valuable <\s>
<s> that the supply we at present want is clothing and arms for twenty five thousand men with a suitable quantity of ammunition and one hundred field pieces <\s>
<s> that we mean to pay for the same by remittances to france or through spain portugal or the french islands as soon as our navigation can be protected by ourselves or friends and that we besides want great quantities of linens and woollens with other articles for the indian trade which you are now actually purchasing and for which you ask no credit and that the whole if france should grant the other supplies would make a cargo which it might be well to secure by a convoy of two or three ships of war <\s>
<s> if you should find m <\s>
<s> de vergennes reserved and not inclined to enter into free conversation with you it may be well to shorten your visit request him to consider what you have proposed acquaint him with your place of lodging that you may yet stay sometime at paris and that knowing how precious his time is you do not presume to ask another audience but that if he should have any commands for you you will upon the least notice immediately wait upon him <\s>
<s> if at a future conference he should be more free and you find a disposition to favor the colonies it may be proper to acquaint him that they must necessarily be anxious to know the disposition of france on certain points which with his permission you would mention such as whether if the colonies should be forced to form themselves into an independent state france would probably acknowledge them as such receive their ambassadors enter into any treaty or alliance with them for commerce or defence or both <\s>
<s> if so on what principal conditions <\s>
<s> intimating that you shall speedily have an opportunity of sending to america if you do not immediately return and that he may be assured of your fidelity and secrecy in transmitting carefully any thing he would wish conveyed to the congress on that subject <\s>
<s> in subsequent conversations you may as you find it convenient enlarge on these topics that have been the subjects of our conferences with you to which you may occasionally add the well known substantial answers we usually give to the several calumnies thrown out against us <\s>
<s> if these supplies on the credit of the congress should be refused you are then to endeavor the obtaining a permission of purchasing those articles or as much of them as you can find credit for <\s>
<s> you will keep a daily journal of all your material transactions and particularly of what passes in your conversation with great personages and you will by every safe opportunity furnish us with such information as may be important <\s>
<s> when your business in france admits of it it may be well to go into holland and visit our agent there m <\s>

<s> passy february 10th 1779 513 note the french money so often mentioned in this and the succeeding volumes is reckoned in livres sols and deniers <\s>
<s> thus 85,706 _l 16_s 3_d or 85,706 <\s>
<s> indicates 85,706 livres 16 sols 3 deniers <\s>
<s> in reducing this money to american currency five livres and eight sols were allowed to the dollar <\s>
<s> the correspondence of silas deane commissioner from the united states to the court of france <\s>
<s> silas deane was born in the town of groton connecticut and graduated at yale college in 1758 <\s>
<s> he was a member from his native colony of the first congress that met in philadelphia <\s>
<s> early in the year 1776 the committee of secret correspondence commissioned him to go to france as a political and commercial agent <\s>
<s> he was instructed to ascertain the disposition of the french court in regard to the contest between great britain and the colonies and to procure if possible supplies of arms and military stores <\s>
<s> having arrived at paris in june he immediately applied himself to execute his instructions and was successful in obtaining the main objects for which he was sent <\s>
<s> in september three commissioners were appointed by congress to negotiate treaties with foreign powers and particularly with the court of france <\s>
<s> the persons chosen were dr franklin silas deane and arthur lee <\s>
<s> they all met at paris in december and continued to procure supplies of money and arms for the united states till at length they signed the treaties of alliance and commerce with france february 6th 1778 <\s>
<s> meantime deane had been recalled on the 21st of november preceding <\s>
<s> of this he received the intelligence in march following and left paris april 1st to join count d'estaing's fleet at toulon in which he came to america <\s>
<s> the account which he gave to congress of his transactions abroad was not satisfactory and he was detained many months in philadelphia soliciting opportunities to vindicate himself before congress from what he deemed the unjust charges of his enemies but the papers relating to his mercantile proceedings having been left in france he was not able wholly to remove the unfavorable impression that existed against him <\s>
<s> congress however neither passed a vote of censure nor approbation of his conduct <\s>
<s> in the spring of 1780 he returned to france where he remained more than a year in reduced circumstances attempting to settle his accounts <\s>
<s> he exhibited large claims against congress which do not appear to have been allowed <\s>
<s> in march 1782 he was living in ghent <\s>
<s> after the peace he went to england where he died in august 1789 <\s>
<s> the correspondence of silas deane <\s>
<s> from the committee of secret correspondence to silas deane 1 philadelphia march 3d 1776 <\s>
<s> on your arrival in france you will for some time be engaged in the business of providing goods for the indian trade <\s>
<s> this will give good countenance to your appearing in the character of a merchant which we wish you continually to retain among the french in general it being probable that the court of france may not like it should be known publicly that any agent from the colonies is in that country <\s>
<s> when you come to paris by delivering dr franklin's letters to monsieur le roy at the louvre and m <\s>
<s> dubourg you will be introduced to a set of acquaintance all friends to the americans <\s>
<s> by conversing with them you will have a good opportunity of acquiring parisian french and you will find in m <\s>
<s> dubourg a man prudent faithful secret intelligent in affairs and capable of giving you very sage advice <\s>
<s> it is scarce necessary to pretend any other business at paris than the gratifying of that curiosity which draws numbers thither yearly merely to see so famous a city <\s>
<s> with the assistance of monsieur dubourg who understands english you will be able to make immediate application to monsieur de vergennes _ministre des affaires etrangères either personally or by letter if m <\s>
<s> dubourg adopts that method acquainting him that you are in france upon business of the american congress in the character of a merchant having something to communicate to him that may be mutually beneficial to france and the north american colonies that you request an audience of him and that he would be pleased to appoint the time and place <\s>
<s> at this audience if agreed to it may be well to show him first your letter of credence and then acquaint him that the congress finding that in the common course of commerce it was not practicable to furnish the continent of america with the quantity of arms and ammunition necessary for its defence the ministry of great britain having been extremely industrious to prevent it you had been despatched by their authority to apply to some european power for a supply <\s>
<s> that france had been pitched on for the first application from an opinion that if we should as there is a great appearance we shall come to a total separation from great britain france would be looked upon as the power whose friendship it would be fittest for us to obtain and cultivate <\s>
<s> that the commercial advantages britain had enjoyed with the colonies had contributed greatly to her late wealth and importance <\s>
<s> that it is likely great part of our commerce will naturally fall to the share of france especially if she favors us in this application as that will be a means of gaining and securing the friendship of the colonies and that as our trade was rapidly increasing with our increase of people and in a greater proportion her part of it will be extremely valuable <\s>
<s> that the supply we at present want is clothing and arms for twenty five thousand men with a suitable quantity of ammunition and one hundred field pieces <\s>
<s> that we mean to pay for the same by remittances to france or through spain portugal or the french islands as soon as our navigation can be protected by ourselves or friends and that we besides want great quantities of linens and woollens with other articles for the indian trade which you are now actually purchasing and for which you ask no credit and that the whole if france should grant the other supplies would make a cargo which it might be well to secure by a convoy of two or three ships of war <\s>
<s> if you should find m <\s>
<s> de vergennes reserved and not inclined to enter into free conversation with you it may be well to shorten your visit request him to consider what you have proposed acquaint him with your place of lodging that you may yet stay sometime at paris and that knowing how precious his time is you do not presume to ask another audience but that if he should have any commands for you you will upon the least notice immediately wait upon him <\s>
<s> if at a future conference he should be more free and you find a disposition to favor the colonies it may be proper to acquaint him that they must necessarily be anxious to know the disposition of france on certain points which with his permission you would mention such as whether if the colonies should be forced to form themselves into an independent state france would probably acknowledge them as such receive their ambassadors enter into any treaty or alliance with them for commerce or defence or both <\s>
<s> if so on what principal conditions <\s>
<s> intimating that you shall speedily have an opportunity of sending to america if you do not immediately return and that he may be assured of your fidelity and secrecy in transmitting carefully any thing he would wish conveyed to the congress on that subject <\s>
<s> in subsequent conversations you may as you find it convenient enlarge on these topics that have been the subjects of our conferences with you to which you may occasionally add the well known substantial answers we usually give to the several calumnies thrown out against us <\s>
<s> if these supplies on the credit of the congress should be refused you are then to endeavor the obtaining a permission of purchasing those articles or as much of them as you can find credit for <\s>
<s> you will keep a daily journal of all your material transactions and particularly of what passes in your conversation with great personages and you will by every safe opportunity furnish us with such information as may be important <\s>
<s> when your business in france admits of it it may be well to go into holland and visit our agent there m <\s>

<s> early in the year 1776 the committee of secret correspondence commissioned him to go to france as a political and commercial agent <\s>

<s> in september three commissioners were appointed by congress to negotiate treaties with foreign powers and particularly with the court of france <\s>
<s> the persons chosen were dr franklin silas deane and arthur lee <\s>
<s> they all met at paris in december and continued to procure supplies of money and arms for the united states till at length they signed the treaties of alliance and commerce with france february 6th 1778 <\s>

<s> of this he received the intelligence in march following and left paris april 1st to join count d'estaing's fleet at toulon in which he came to america <\s>
<s> the account which he gave to congress of his transactions abroad was not satisfactory and he was detained many months in philadelphia soliciting opportunities to vindicate himself before congress from what he deemed the unjust charges of his enemies but the papers relating to his mercantile proceedings having been left in france he was not able wholly to remove the unfavorable impression that existed against him <\s>

<s> in the spring of 1780 he returned to france where he remained more than a year in reduced circumstances attempting to settle his accounts <\s>

<s> in march 1782 he was living in ghent <\s>
<s> after the peace he went to england where he died in august 1789 <\s>

<s> from the committee of secret correspondence to silas deane 1 philadelphia march 3d 1776 <\s>
<s> on your arrival in france you will for some time be engaged in the business of providing goods for the indian trade <\s>
<s> this will give good countenance to your appearing in the character of a merchant which we wish you continually to retain among the french in general it being probable that the court of france may not like it should be known publicly that any agent from the colonies is in that country <\s>
<s> when you come to paris by delivering dr franklin's letters to monsieur le roy at the louvre and m <\s>
<s> dubourg you will be introduced to a set of acquaintance all friends to the americans <\s>
<s> by conversing with them you will have a good opportunity of acquiring parisian french and you will find in m <\s>
<s> dubourg a man prudent faithful secret intelligent in affairs and capable of giving you very sage advice <\s>
<s> it is scarce necessary to pretend any other business at paris than the gratifying of that curiosity which draws numbers thither yearly merely to see so famous a city <\s>
<s> with the assistance of monsieur dubourg who understands english you will be able to make immediate application to monsieur de vergennes _ministre des affaires etrangères either personally or by letter if m <\s>
<s> dubourg adopts that method acquainting him that you are in france upon business of the american congress in the character of a merchant having something to communicate to him that may be mutually beneficial to france and the north american colonies that you request an audience of him and that he would be pleased to appoint the time and place <\s>
<s> at this audience if agreed to it may be well to show him first your letter of credence and then acquaint him that the congress finding that in the common course of commerce it was not practicable to furnish the continent of america with the quantity of arms and ammunition necessary for its defence the ministry of great britain having been extremely industrious to prevent it you had been despatched by their authority to apply to some european power for a supply <\s>
<s> that france had been pitched on for the first application from an opinion that if we should as there is a great appearance we shall come to a total separation from great britain france would be looked upon as the power whose friendship it would be fittest for us to obtain and cultivate <\s>
<s> that the commercial advantages britain had enjoyed with the colonies had contributed greatly to her late wealth and importance <\s>
<s> that it is likely great part of our commerce will naturally fall to the share of france especially if she favors us in this application as that will be a means of gaining and securing the friendship of the colonies and that as our trade was rapidly increasing with our increase of people and in a greater proportion her part of it will be extremely valuable <\s>
<s> that the supply we at present want is clothing and arms for twenty five thousand men with a suitable quantity of ammunition and one hundred field pieces <\s>
<s> that we mean to pay for the same by remittances to france or through spain portugal or the french islands as soon as our navigation can be protected by ourselves or friends and that we besides want great quantities of linens and woollens with other articles for the indian trade which you are now actually purchasing and for which you ask no credit and that the whole if france should grant the other supplies would make a cargo which it might be well to secure by a convoy of two or three ships of war <\s>
<s> if you should find m <\s>
<s> de vergennes reserved and not inclined to enter into free conversation with you it may be well to shorten your visit request him to consider what you have proposed acquaint him with your place of lodging that you may yet stay sometime at paris and that knowing how precious his time is you do not presume to ask another audience but that if he should have any commands for you you will upon the least notice immediately wait upon him <\s>
<s> if at a future conference he should be more free and you find a disposition to favor the colonies it may be proper to acquaint him that they must necessarily be anxious to know the disposition of france on certain points which with his permission you would mention such as whether if the colonies should be forced to form themselves into an independent state france would probably acknowledge them as such receive their ambassadors enter into any treaty or alliance with them for commerce or defence or both <\s>
<s> if so on what principal conditions <\s>
<s> intimating that you shall speedily have an opportunity of sending to america if you do not immediately return and that he may be assured of your fidelity and secrecy in transmitting carefully any thing he would wish conveyed to the congress on that subject <\s>
<s> in subsequent conversations you may as you find it convenient enlarge on these topics that have been the subjects of our conferences with you to which you may occasionally add the well known substantial answers we usually give to the several calumnies thrown out against us <\s>
<s> if these supplies on the credit of the congress should be refused you are then to endeavor the obtaining a permission of purchasing those articles or as much of them as you can find credit for <\s>
<s> you will keep a daily journal of all your material transactions and particularly of what passes in your conversation with great personages and you will by every safe opportunity furnish us with such information as may be important <\s>
<s> when your business in france admits of it it may be well to go into holland and visit our agent there m <\s>

<s> on your arrival in france you will for some time be engaged in the business of providing goods for the indian trade <\s>
<s> this will give good countenance to your appearing in the character of a merchant which we wish you continually to retain among the french in general it being probable that the court of france may not like it should be known publicly that any agent from the colonies is in that country <\s>
<s> when you come to paris by delivering dr franklin's letters to monsieur le roy at the louvre and m <\s>
<s> dubourg you will be introduced to a set of acquaintance all friends to the americans <\s>
<s> by conversing with them you will have a good opportunity of acquiring parisian french and you will find in m <\s>
<s> dubourg a man prudent faithful secret intelligent in affairs and capable of giving you very sage advice <\s>
<s> it is scarce necessary to pretend any other business at paris than the gratifying of that curiosity which draws numbers thither yearly merely to see so famous a city <\s>
<s> with the assistance of monsieur dubourg who understands english you will be able to make immediate application to monsieur de vergennes _ministre des affaires etrangères either personally or by letter if m <\s>
<s> dubourg adopts that method acquainting him that you are in france upon business of the american congress in the character of a merchant having something to communicate to him that may be mutually beneficial to france and the north american colonies that you request an audience of him and that he would be pleased to appoint the time and place <\s>
<s> at this audience if agreed to it may be well to show him first your letter of credence and then acquaint him that the congress finding that in the common course of commerce it was not practicable to furnish the continent of america with the quantity of arms and ammunition necessary for its defence the ministry of great britain having been extremely industrious to prevent it you had been despatched by their authority to apply to some european power for a supply <\s>
<s> that france had been pitched on for the first application from an opinion that if we should as there is a great appearance we shall come to a total separation from great britain france would be looked upon as the power whose friendship it would be fittest for us to obtain and cultivate <\s>
<s> that the commercial advantages britain had enjoyed with the colonies had contributed greatly to her late wealth and importance <\s>
<s> that it is likely great part of our commerce will naturally fall to the share of france especially if she favors us in this application as that will be a means of gaining and securing the friendship of the colonies and that as our trade was rapidly increasing with our increase of people and in a greater proportion her part of it will be extremely valuable <\s>
<s> that the supply we at present want is clothing and arms for twenty five thousand men with a suitable quantity of ammunition and one hundred field pieces <\s>
<s> that we mean to pay for the same by remittances to france or through spain portugal or the french islands as soon as our navigation can be protected by ourselves or friends and that we besides want great quantities of linens and woollens with other articles for the indian trade which you are now actually purchasing and for which you ask no credit and that the whole if france should grant the other supplies would make a cargo which it might be well to secure by a convoy of two or three ships of war <\s>
<s> if you should find m <\s>
<s> de vergennes reserved and not inclined to enter into free conversation with you it may be well to shorten your visit request him to consider what you have proposed acquaint him with your place of lodging that you may yet stay sometime at paris and that knowing how precious his time is you do not presume to ask another audience but that if he should have any commands for you you will upon the least notice immediately wait upon him <\s>
<s> if at a future conference he should be more free and you find a disposition to favor the colonies it may be proper to acquaint him that they must necessarily be anxious to know the disposition of france on certain points which with his permission you would mention such as whether if the colonies should be forced to form themselves into an independent state france would probably acknowledge them as such receive their ambassadors enter into any treaty or alliance with them for commerce or defence or both <\s>
<s> if so on what principal conditions <\s>
<s> intimating that you shall speedily have an opportunity of sending to america if you do not immediately return and that he may be assured of your fidelity and secrecy in transmitting carefully any thing he would wish conveyed to the congress on that subject <\s>
<s> in subsequent conversations you may as you find it convenient enlarge on these topics that have been the subjects of our conferences with you to which you may occasionally add the well known substantial answers we usually give to the several calumnies thrown out against us <\s>
<s> if these supplies on the credit of the congress should be refused you are then to endeavor the obtaining a permission of purchasing those articles or as much of them as you can find credit for <\s>
<s> you will keep a daily journal of all your material transactions and particularly of what passes in your conversation with great personages and you will by every safe opportunity furnish us with such information as may be important <\s>
<s> when your business in france admits of it it may be well to go into holland and visit our agent there m <\s>
